    26	func testEnforce(t *testing.T, e *Enforcer, sub interface{}, obj interface{}, act string, res bool) {
    27	        t.Helper()
    28	        if myRes, err := e.Enforce(sub, obj, act); err != nil {
    29	                t.Errorf("Enforce Error: %s", err)
    30	        } else if myRes != res {
    31	                t.Errorf("%s, %v, %s: %t, supposed to be %t", sub, obj, act, myRes, res)
    32	        }
    33	}

    31	
    32	// Model represents the whole access control model.
    33	type Model map[string]AssertionMap
    34	
    35	// AssertionMap is the collection of assertions, can be "r", "p", "g", "e", "m".
    36	type AssertionMap map[string]*Assertion
    37	
    38	const defaultDomain string = ""
    39	const defaultSeparator = "::"
    40	
    41	var sectionNameMap = map[string]string{
    42	        "r": "request_definition",
    43	        "p": "policy_definition",
    44	        "g": "role_definition",
    45	        "e": "policy_effect",
    46	        "m": "matchers",
    47	}
    48	
    49	// Minimal required sections for a model to be valid.
    50	var requiredSections = []string{"r", "p", "e", "m"}
    51	
    52	func loadAssertion(model Model, cfg config.ConfigInterface, sec string, key string) bool {
    53	        value := cfg.String(sectionNameMap[sec] + "::" + key)
    54	        return model.AddDef(sec, key, value)
    55	}
    56	
    57	var paramsRegex = regexp.MustCompile(`\((.*?)\)`)
    58	
    59	// getParamsToken Get ParamsToken from Assertion.Value.
    60	func getParamsToken(value string) []string {
    61	        paramsString := paramsRegex.FindString(value)
    62	        if paramsString == "" {
    63	                return nil
    64	        }
    65	        paramsString = strings.TrimSuffix(strings.TrimPrefix(paramsString, "("), ")")
    66	        return strings.Split(paramsString, ",")
    67	}
    68	
    69	// AddDef adds an assertion to the model.
    70	func (model Model) AddDef(sec string, key string, value string) bool {
    71	        if value == "" {
    72	                return false
    73	        }
    74	
    75	        ast := Assertion{}
    76	        ast.Key = key
    77	        ast.Value = value
    78	        ast.PolicyMap = make(map[string]int)
    79	        ast.FieldIndexMap = make(map[string]int)
    80	        ast.setLogger(model.GetLogger())
    81	
    82	        if sec == "r" || sec == "p" {
    83	                ast.Tokens = strings.Split(ast.Value, ",")
    84	                for i := range ast.Tokens {
    85	                        ast.Tokens[i] = key + "_" + strings.TrimSpace(ast.Tokens[i])
    86	                }
    87	        } else if sec == "g" {
    88	                ast.ParamsTokens = getParamsToken(ast.Value)
    89	                ast.Tokens = strings.Split(ast.Value, ",")
    90	                ast.Tokens = ast.Tokens[:len(ast.Tokens)-len(ast.ParamsTokens)]
    91	        } else {
    92	                ast.Value = util.RemoveComments(util.EscapeAssertion(ast.Value))
    93	        }
    94	
    95	        if sec == "m" && strings.Contains(ast.Value, "in") {
    96	                ast.Value = strings.Replace(strings.Replace(ast.Value, "[", "(", -1), "]", ")", -1)
    97	        }
    98	
    99	        _, ok := model[sec]
   100	        if !ok {

str_replace_editor create /testbed/blp_research.md --file_text '# BLP (Bell-LaPadula) Model Research

## What is BLP?
The Bell-LaPadula model is a formal state transition model for computer security policy that describes a set of access control rules using security labels on objects and clearances for subjects.

## Key Principles:
1. **Simple Security Property (no read up)**: A subject at a given security level cannot read an object at a higher security level.
2. **-Property (no write down)**: A subject at a given security level cannot write to any object at a lower security level.

## Security Levels:
Typically classified as: Unclassified, Confidential, Secret, Top Secret

## Comparison with ReBAC:
- ReBAC (Relationship-Based Access Control) uses relationships between entities
- BLP uses security labels and clearances

## How BLP might work in Casbin:
- Subjects have clearance levels (e.g., secret, confidential)
- Objects have classification levels (e.g., top secret, secret)
- Policies enforce the BLP rules

## Possible Model Structure:
[request_definition]
r = sub, obj, act

[policy_definition] 
p = sub_level, obj_level, act

[role_definition]
(or maybe custom functions for level comparison)

[matchers]
m = some function to check BLP rules

## Key Difference from ReBAC:
ReBAC uses relationships (g, g2 functions), BLP uses hierarchy comparison'

   204	func KeyMatch3Func(args ...interface{}) (interface{}, error) {
   205	        if err := validateVariadicArgs(2, args...); err != nil {
   206	                return false, fmt.Errorf("%s: %w", "keyMatch3", err)
   207	        }

   215	// KeyGet3 returns value matched pattern
   216	// For example, "project/proj_project1_admin/" matches "project/proj_{project}_admin/"
   217	// if the pathVar == "project", then "project1" will be returned.
   218	func KeyGet3(key1, key2 string, pathVar string) string {
   219	        key2 = strings.Replace(key2, "/*", "/.*", -1)
   220	
   221	        keys := keyGet3Re1.FindAllString(key2, -1)
   222	        key2 = keyGet3Re1.ReplaceAllString(key2, "$1([^/]+?)$2")
   223	        key2 = "^" + key2 + "$"
   224	        re := mustCompileOrGet(key2)
   225	        values := re.FindAllStringSubmatch(key1, -1)
   226	        if len(values) == 0 {
   227	                return ""
   228	        }
   229	        for i, key := range keys {
   230	                if pathVar == key[1:len(key)-1] {
   231	                        return values[0][i+1]
   232	                }
   233	        }
   234	        return ""
   235	}
   236

   240	                return false, fmt.Errorf("%s: %w", "keyGet3", err)

   250	// KeyMatch4 determines whether key1 matches the pattern of key2 (similar to RESTful path), key2 can contain a *.
   251	// Besides what KeyMatch3 does, KeyMatch4 can also match repeated patterns:
   252	// "/parent/123/child/123" matches "/parent/{id}/child/{id}"
   253	// "/parent/123/child/456" does not match "/parent/{id}/child/{id}"
   254	// But KeyMatch3 will match both.
   255	func KeyMatch4(key1 string, key2 string) bool {
   256	        key2 = strings.Replace(key2, "/*", "/.*", -1)

   262	                tokens = append(tokens, s[1:len(s)-1])
   263	                return "([^/]+)"
   264	        })
   265	
   266	        re = mustCompileOrGet("^" + key2 + "$")

   269	                return false
   270	        }
   271	        matches = matches[1:]
   272	
   273	        if len(tokens) != len(matches) {
   274	                panic(errors.New("KeyMatch4: number of tokens is not equal to number of values"))

    27	}

    29	// [string]govaluate.ExpressionFunction
    30	
    31	// AddFunction adds an expression function.
    32	func (fm *FunctionMap) AddFunction(name string, function govaluate.ExpressionFunction) {
    33	        fm.fns.LoadOrStore(name, function)
    34	}
    35	
    36	// LoadFunctionMap loads an initial function map.
    37	func LoadFunctionMap() FunctionMap {
    38	        fm := &FunctionMap{}
    39	        fm.fns = &sync.Map{}
    40	
    41	        fm.AddFunction("keyMatch", util.KeyMatchFunc)
    42	        fm.AddFunction("keyGet", util.KeyGetFunc)
    43	        fm.AddFunction("keyMatch2", util.KeyMatch2Func)
    44	        fm.AddFunction("keyGet2", util.KeyGet2Func)
    45	        fm.AddFunction("keyMatch3", util.KeyMatch3Func)
    46	        fm.AddFunction("keyGet3", util.KeyGet3Func)
    47	        fm.AddFunction("keyMatch4", util.KeyMatch4Func)
    48	        fm.AddFunction("keyMatch5", util.KeyMatch5Func)
    49	        fm.AddFunction("regexMatch", util.RegexMatchFunc)
    50	        fm.AddFunction("ipMatch", util.IPMatchFunc)
    51	        fm.AddFunction("globMatch", util.GlobMatchFunc)
    52	
    53	        return *fm
    54	}
    55	
    56	// GetFunctions return a map with all the functions.
    57	func (fm *FunctionMap) GetFunctions() map[string]govaluate.ExpressionFunction {
    58	        ret := make(map[string]govaluate.ExpressionFunction)
    59	
    60	        fm.fns.Range(func(k interface{}, v interface{}) bool {
    61	                ret[k.(string)] = v.(govaluate.ExpressionFunction)
    62	                return true
    63	        })
    64	
    65	        return ret
    66	}

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor create /testbed/test_blp_implementation.go --file_text 'package main

import (
	"fmt"
	"github.com/casbin/casbin/v2"
	"github.com/casbin/casbin/v2/util"
	"github.com/casbin/govaluate"
)

// Security level hierarchy (from low to high)
var securityLevels = map[string]int{
	"public":       0,
	"confidential": 1,
	"secret":       2,
	"top_secret":   3,
}

// security_level_lte function for BLP model
func securityLevelLteFunc(args ...interface{}) (interface{}, error) {
	if len(args) != 2 {
		return false, fmt.Errorf("security_level_lte requires exactly 2 arguments")
	}
	
	level1, ok1 := args[0].(string)
	level2, ok2 := args[1].(string)
	
	if !ok1 || !ok2 {
		return false, fmt.Errorf("security_level_lte requires string arguments")
	}
	
	num1, exists1 := securityLevels[level1]
	num2, exists2 := securityLevels[level2]
	
	if !exists1 || !exists2 {
		return false, fmt.Errorf("unknown security level")
	}
	
	return num1 <= num2, nil
}

func main() {
	// Create a new enforcer
	e, err := casbin.NewEnforcer("examples/blp_model.conf", "examples/blp_policy.csv")
	if err != nil {
		panic(err)
	}

	// Add the custom security level function
	e.AddFunction("security_level_lte", securityLevelLteFunc)

	// Test cases based on BLP rules
	testCases := []struct {
		sub  string
		obj  string
		act  string
		want bool
	}{
		// Alice (secret) trying to read doc1 (confidential) - allowed
		{"alice", "doc1", "read", true},
		// Alice (secret) trying to read doc2 (secret) - allowed  
		{"alice", "doc2", "read", true},
		// Alice (secret) trying to read doc3 (top_secret) - denied (no read up)
		{"alice", "doc3", "read", false},
		// Alice (secret) trying to write doc1 (confidential) - denied (no write down)
		{"alice", "doc1", "write", false},
		// Alice (secret) trying to write doc2 (secret) - allowed
		{"alice", "doc2", "write", true},
		
		// Bob (top_secret) trying to read doc1 (confidential) - allowed
		{"bob", "doc1", "read", true},
		// Bob (top_secret) trying to read doc2 (secret) - allowed
		{"bob", "doc2", "read", true},
		// Bob (top_secret) trying to read doc3 (top_secret) - allowed
		{"bob", "doc3", "read", true},
		// Bob (top_secret) trying to write doc1 (confidential) - denied (no write down)
		{"bob", "doc1", "write", false},
		// Bob (top_secret) trying to write doc2 (secret) - denied (no write down)
		{"bob", "doc2", "write", false},
		// Bob (top_secret) trying to write doc3 (top_secret) - allowed
		{"bob", "doc3", "write", true},
	}

	fmt.Println("Testing BLP model:")
	fmt.Println("Security levels: public(0) < confidential(1) < secret(2) < top_secret(3)")
	fmt.Println("Subjects: alice=secret, bob=top_secret")
	fmt.Println("Objects: doc1=confidential, doc2=secret, doc3=top_secret")
	fmt.Println()

	for i, tc := range testCases {
		got, err := e.Enforce(tc.sub, tc.obj, tc.act)
		if err != nil {
			fmt.Printf("Test %d (%s, %s, %s): ERROR - %v\n", i+1, tc.sub, tc.obj, tc.act, err)
		} else if got != tc.want {
			fmt.Printf("Test %d (%s, %s, %s): FAIL - got %t, want %t\n", i+1, tc.sub, tc.obj, tc.act, got, tc.want)
		} else {
			fmt.Printf("Test %d (%s, %s, %s): PASS\n", i+1, tc.sub, tc.obj, tc.act)
		}
	}
}'

var securityLevels = map[string]int{
	"public":       0,
	"confidential": 1,
	"secret":       2,
	"top_secret":   3,
}

// security_level_lte function for BLP model
func securityLevelLteFunc(args ...interface{}) (interface{}, error) {
	if len(args) != 2 {
		return false, fmt.Errorf("security_level_lte requires exactly 2 arguments")
	}
	
	level1, ok1 := args[0].(string)
	level2, ok2 := args[1].(string)
	
	if !ok1 || !ok2 {
		return false, fmt.Errorf("security_level_lte requires string arguments")
	}
	
	num1, exists1 := securityLevels[level1]
	num2, exists2 := securityLevels[level2]
	
	if !exists1 || !exists2 {
		return false, fmt.Errorf("unknown security level")
	}
	
	return num1 <= num2, nil
}

func main() {
	// Create a new enforcer
	e, err := casbin.NewEnforcer("examples/blp_model.conf", "examples/blp_policy.csv")
	if err != nil {
		panic(err)
	}

	// Add the custom security level function
	e.AddFunction("security_level_lte", securityLevelLteFunc)

	// Test cases based on BLP rules
	testCases := []struct {
		sub  string
		obj  string
		act  string
		want bool
	}{
		// Alice (secret) trying to read doc1 (confidential) - allowed
		{"alice", "doc1", "read", true},
		// Alice (secret) trying to read doc2 (secret) - allowed  
		{"alice", "doc2", "read", true},
		// Alice (secret) trying to read doc3 (top_secret) - denied (no read up)
		{"alice", "doc3", "read", false},
		// Alice (secret) trying to write doc1 (confidential) - denied (no write down)
		{"alice", "doc1", "write", false},
		// Alice (secret) trying to write doc2 (secret) - allowed
		{"alice", "doc2", "write", true},
		
		// Bob (top_secret) trying to read doc1 (confidential) - allowed
		{"bob", "doc1", "read", true},
		// Bob (top_secret) trying to read doc2 (secret) - allowed
		{"bob", "doc2", "read", true},
		// Bob (top_secret) trying to read doc3 (top_secret) - allowed
		{"bob", "doc3", "read", true},
		// Bob (top_secret) trying to write doc1 (confidential) - denied (no write down)
		{"bob", "doc1", "write", false},
		// Bob (top_secret) trying to write doc2 (secret) - denied (no write down)
		{"bob", "doc2", "write", false},
		// Bob (top_secret) trying to write doc3 (top_secret) - allowed
		{"bob", "doc3", "write", true},
	}

	fmt.Println("Testing BLP model:")
	fmt.Println("Security levels: public(0) < confidential(1) < secret(2) < top_secret(3)")
	fmt.Println("Subjects: alice=secret, bob=top_secret")
	fmt.Println("Objects: doc1=confidential, doc2=secret, doc3=top_secret")
	fmt.Println()

	for i, tc := range testCases {
		got, err := e.Enforce(tc.sub, tc.obj, tc.act)
		if err != nil {
			fmt.Printf("Test %d (%s, %s, %s): ERROR - %v\n", i+1, tc.sub, tc.obj, tc.act, err)
		} else if got != tc.want {
			fmt.Printf("Test %d (%s, %s, %s): FAIL - got %t, want %t\n", i+1, tc.sub, tc.obj, tc.act, got, tc.want)
		} else {
			fmt.Printf("Test %d (%s, %s, %s): PASS\n", i+1, tc.sub, tc.obj, tc.act)
		}
	}

import (
	"fmt"
	"github.com/casbin/casbin/v2"
)

func main() {
	// Create a new enforcer
	e, err := casbin.NewEnforcer("examples/blp_model.conf", "examples/blp_policy.csv")
	if err != nil {
		panic(err)
	}

	// Test cases based on BLP rules
	testCases := []struct {
		sub  string
		obj  string
		act  string
		want bool
	}{
		// Alice (secret) trying to read doc1 (confidential) - allowed (no read up)
		{"alice", "doc1", "read", true},
		// Alice (secret) trying to read doc2 (secret) - allowed
		{"alice", "doc2", "read", true},
		// Alice (secret) trying to read doc3 (top_secret) - denied (no read up)
		{"alice", "doc3", "read", false},
		// Alice (secret) trying to write doc1 (confidential) - denied (no write down)
		{"alice", "doc1", "write", false},
		// Alice (secret) trying to write doc2 (secret) - allowed
		{"alice", "doc2", "write", true},
		
		// Bob (top_secret) trying to read doc1 (confidential) - allowed
		{"bob", "doc1", "read", true},
		// Bob (top_secret) trying to read doc2 (secret) - allowed
		{"bob", "doc2", "read", true},
		// Bob (top_secret) trying to read doc3 (top_secret) - allowed
		{"bob", "doc3", "read", true},
		// Bob (top_secret) trying to write doc1 (confidential) - denied (no write down)
		{"bob", "doc1", "write", false},
		// Bob (top_secret) trying to write doc2 (secret) - denied (no write down)
		{"bob", "doc2", "write", false},
		// Bob (top_secret) trying to write doc3 (top_secret) - allowed
		{"bob", "doc3", "write", true},
	}

	fmt.Println("Testing BLP model:")
	fmt.Println("Security levels: confidential < secret < top_secret")
	fmt.Println("Subjects: alice=secret, bob=top_secret")
	fmt.Println("Objects: doc1=confidential, doc2=secret, doc3=top_secret")
	fmt.Println()

	for i, tc := range testCases {
		got, err := e.Enforce(tc.sub, tc.obj, tc.act)
		if err != nil {
			fmt.Printf("Test %d (%s, %s, %s): ERROR - %v\n", i+1, tc.sub, tc.obj, tc.act, err)
		} else if got != tc.want {
			fmt.Printf("Test %d (%s, %s, %s): FAIL - got %t, want %t\n", i+1, tc.sub, tc.obj, tc.act, got, tc.want)
		} else {
			fmt.Printf("Test %d (%s, %s, %s): PASS\n", i+1, tc.sub, tc.obj, tc.act)
		}
	}
}'

	// Test BLP model rules
	// Security levels: confidential < secret < top_secret
	// Alice has secret clearance, Bob has top_secret clearance
	// doc1 is confidential, doc2 is secret, doc3 is top_secret

	// Alice (secret) trying to read doc1 (confidential) - allowed (no read up)

	// Alice (secret) trying to read doc2 (secret) - allowed

// Test BLP model rules
// Security levels: confidential < secret < top_secret
// Alice has secret clearance, Bob has top_secret clearance
// doc1 is confidential, doc2 is secret, doc3 is top_secret

// Alice (secret) trying to read doc1 (confidential) - allowed (no read up)
testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "doc1", "read", true)
// Alice (secret) trying to read doc2 (secret) - allowed
testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "doc2", "read", true)
// Alice (secret) trying to read doc3 (top_secret) - denied (no read up)
testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "doc3", "read", false)
// Alice (secret) trying to write doc1 (confidential) - denied (no write down)
testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "doc1", "write", false)
// Alice (secret) trying to write doc2 (secret) - allowed
testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "doc2", "write", true)

// Bob (top_secret) trying to read doc1 (confidential) - allowed
testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "doc1", "read", true)
// Bob (top_secret) trying to read doc2 (secret) - allowed
testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "doc2", "read", true)
// Bob (top_secret) trying to read doc3 (top_secret) - allowed
testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "doc3", "read", true)
// Bob (top_secret) trying to write doc1 (confidential) - denied (no write down)
testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "doc1", "write", false)
// Bob (top_secret) trying to write doc2 (secret) - denied (no write down)

+        // Here's a little confusing: the matching function here is not the custom function used in matcher.
+        // It is the matching function used by "g" (and "g2", "g3" if any..)
+        // You can see in policy that: "g2, /book/:id, book_group", so in "g2()" function in the matcher, instead
+        // of checking whether "/book/:id" equals the obj: "/book/1", it checks whether the pattern matches.
+        // You can see it as normal RBAC: "/book/:id" == "/book/1" becomes KeyMatch2("/book/:id", "/book/1")
+        e.AddNamedMatchingFunc("g2", "KeyMatch2", util.KeyMatch2)
+        e.AddNamedMatchingFunc("g", "KeyMatch2", util.KeyMatch2)

+

+        testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "/book/1", "GET", false)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "/book/2", "GET", false)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "/pen/1", "GET", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "/pen/2", "GET", true)
+
+        // AddMatchingFunc() is actually setting a function because only one function is allowed,
+        // so when we set "KeyMatch3", we are actually replacing "KeyMatch2" with "KeyMatch3".
+        e.AddNamedMatchingFunc("g2", "KeyMatch2", util.KeyMatch3)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/book2/1", "GET", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/book2/2", "GET", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/pen2/1", "GET", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/pen2/2", "GET", false)

+# Security levels hierarchy (from low to high): confidential < secret < top_secret
+
+# Define hierarchy of security levels - lower levels inherit from higher levels

+g, secret, top_secret
+
+# Assign subjects to security levels
+g, alice, secret
+g, bob, top_secret
+
+# Assign objects to security levels
+g, doc1, confidential
+g, doc2, secret
+g, doc3, top_secret
+
+# Allow actions between security levels following BLP rules
+# Read: subject_level >= object_level allowed
+# Write: subject_level <= object_level allowed

+        e, _ := NewEnforcer("examples/rbac_with_pattern_model.conf", "examples/rbac_with_pattern_policy.csv")
+
+        // Here's a little confusing: the matching function here is not the custom function used in matcher.
+        // It is the matching function used by "g" (and "g2", "g3" if any..)
+        // You can see in policy that: "g2, /book/:id, book_group", so in "g2()" function in the matcher, instead
+        // of checking whether "/book/:id" equals the obj: "/book/1", it checks whether the pattern matches.
+        // You can see it as normal RBAC: "/book/:id" == "/book/1" becomes KeyMatch2("/book/:id", "/book/1")
+        e.AddNamedMatchingFunc("g2", "KeyMatch2", util.KeyMatch2)
+        e.AddNamedMatchingFunc("g", "KeyMatch2", util.KeyMatch2)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "any_user", "/pen3/1", "GET", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "/book/user/1", "/pen4/1", "GET", true)
+
+        testEnforce(t, e, "/book/user/1", "/pen4/1", "POST", true)
+
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/book/1", "GET", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/book/2", "GET", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/pen/1", "GET", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/pen/2", "GET", false)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "/book/1", "GET", false)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "/book/2", "GET", false)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "/pen/1", "GET", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "/pen/2", "GET", true)
+
+        // AddMatchingFunc() is actually setting a function because only one function is allowed,
+        // so when we set "KeyMatch3", we are actually replacing "KeyMatch2" with "KeyMatch3".
+        e.AddNamedMatchingFunc("g2", "KeyMatch2", util.KeyMatch3)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/book2/1", "GET", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/book2/2", "GET", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/pen2/1", "GET", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/pen2/2", "GET", false)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "/book2/1", "GET", false)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "/book2/2", "GET", false)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "/pen2/1", "GET", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "/pen2/2", "GET", true)

+func TestBLPModel(t *testing.T) {
+// Check if the BLP model file exists before attempting to load
+e, err := NewEnforcer("examples/blp_model.conf", "examples/blp_policy.csv")
+if err != nil {
+This indicates the files don't exist or there's a syntax error - create basic test
+model files not initialized yet: %v", err)
+
+}
+
+// Test BLP model rules
+// Security levels: confidential < secret < top_secret
+// Alice has secret clearance, Bob has top_secret clearance
+// doc1 is confidential, doc2 is secret, doc3 is top_secret
+
+// Alice (secret) trying to read doc1 (confidential) - allowed (no read up)
+testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "doc1", "read", true)
+// Alice (secret) trying to read doc2 (secret) - allowed
+testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "doc2", "read", true)
+// Alice (secret) trying to read doc3 (top_secret) - denied (no read up)
+testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "doc3", "read", false)
+// Alice (secret) trying to write doc1 (confidential) - denied (no write down)
+testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "doc1", "write", false)
+// Alice (secret) trying to write doc2 (secret) - allowed
+testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "doc2", "write", true)
+
+// Bob (top_secret) trying to read doc1 (confidential) - allowed
+testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "doc1", "read", true)
+// Bob (top_secret) trying to read doc2 (secret) - allowed
+testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "doc2", "read", true)
+// Bob (top_secret) trying to read doc3 (top_secret) - allowed
+testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "doc3", "read", true)
+// Bob (top_secret) trying to write doc1 (confidential) - denied (no write down)
+testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "doc1", "write", false)
+// Bob (top_secret) trying to write doc2 (secret) - denied (no write down)
+testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "doc2", "write", false)
+// Bob (top_secret) trying to write doc3 (top_secret) - allowed
+testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "doc3", "write", true)
 }

+[request_definition]
+r = sub, obj, act
+
+[policy_definition]
+p = sub, obj, act
+
+[role_definition]
+# Define security level hierarchy - lower levels can inherit from higher levels
+g = _, _
+
+[policy_effect]
+e = some(where (p.eft == allow))
+
+[matchers]
+# BLP model implementation using RBAC hierarchy
+# Subjects and objects are assigned to security levels via g rules
+# Simple Security Property: subject can read object if subject_level >= object_level
+# *-Property: subject can write object if subject_level <= object_level
+m = r.act == p.act && g(r.sub, p.sub) && g(r.obj, p.obj) && (
+    (r.act == "read" && g(p.obj, p.sub)) || 
+    (r.act == "write" && g(p.sub, p.obj))

+# Security levels hierarchy (from low to high): confidential < secret < top_secret
+
+# Define hierarchy of security levels - lower levels inherit from higher levels
+g, confidential, secret
+g, secret, top_secret
+
+# Assign subjects to security levels
+g, alice, secret
+g, bob, top_secret
+
+# Assign objects to security levels
+g, doc1, confidential
+g, doc2, secret
+g, doc3, top_secret
+
+# Allow actions between security levels following BLP rules
+# Read: subject_level >= object_level allowed
+# Write: subject_level <= object_level allowed
+p, secret, confidential, read
+p, secret, secret, read
+p, secret, secret, write
+p, top_secret, confidential, read
+p, top_secret, secret, read
+p, top_secret, secret, write
+p, top_secret, top_secret, read

+        _, _ = e.AddPolicy("admin", "domain2", "data2", "write")

+        _, _ = e.AddGroupingPolicy("alice", "admin", "domain1")
+        _, _ = e.AddGroupingPolicy("bob", "admin", "domain2")
+

+        testDomainEnforce(t, e, "alice", "domain1", "data1", "write", true)

+        testDomainEnforce(t, e, "bob", "domain2", "data2", "write", true)
+
+        // Remove all policy rules related to domain1 and data1.
+        _, _ = e.RemoveFilteredPolicy(1, "domain1", "data1")
+
+        testDomainEnforce(t, e, "alice", "domain1", "data1", "read", false)
+        testDomainEnforce(t, e, "alice", "domain1", "data1", "write", false)

+        testDomainEnforce(t, e, "alice", "domain1", "data2", "write", false)
+        testDomainEnforce(t, e, "bob", "domain2", "data1", "read", false)
+        testDomainEnforce(t, e, "bob", "domain2", "data1", "write", false)
+        testDomainEnforce(t, e, "bob", "domain2", "data2", "read", true)
+        testDomainEnforce(t, e, "bob", "domain2", "data2", "write", true)
+
+        // Remove the specified policy rule.
+        _, _ = e.RemovePolicy("admin", "domain2", "data2", "read")
+
+        testDomainEnforce(t, e, "alice", "domain1", "data1", "read", false)
+        testDomainEnforce(t, e, "alice", "domain1", "data1", "write", false)
+        testDomainEnforce(t, e, "alice", "domain1", "data2", "read", false)
+        testDomainEnforce(t, e, "alice", "domain1", "data2", "write", false)
+        testDomainEnforce(t, e, "bob", "domain2", "data1", "read", false)
+        testDomainEnforce(t, e, "bob", "domain2", "data1", "write", false)
+        testDomainEnforce(t, e, "bob", "domain2", "data2", "read", false)
+        testDomainEnforce(t, e, "bob", "domain2", "data2", "write", true)

 func TestRBACModelWithCustomData(t *testing.T) {
-	e, _ := NewEnforcer("examples/rbac_model.conf", "examples/rbac_policy.csv")
-
-	// You can add custom data to a grouping policy, Casbin will ignore it. It is only meaningful to the caller.
-	// This feature can be used to store information like whether "bob" is an end user (so no subject will inherit "bob")
-	// For Casbin, it is equivalent to: e.AddGroupingPolicy("bob", "data2_admin")
-	_, _ = e.AddGroupingPolicy("bob", "data2_admin", "custom_data")
-
-	testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "data1", "read", true)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "data1", "write", false)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "data2", "read", true)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "data2", "write", true)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "data1", "read", false)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "data1", "write", false)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "data2", "read", true)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "data2", "write", true)
-
-	// You should also take the custom data as a parameter when deleting a grouping policy.
-	// e.RemoveGroupingPolicy("bob", "data2_admin") won't work.
-	// Or you can remove it by using RemoveFilteredGroupingPolicy().
-	_, _ = e.RemoveGroupingPolicy("bob", "data2_admin", "custom_data")
-
-	testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "data1", "read", true)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "data1", "write", false)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "data2", "read", true)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "data2", "write", true)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "data1", "read", false)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "data1", "write", false)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "data2", "read", false)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "data2", "write", true)
+        e, _ := NewEnforcer("examples/rbac_model.conf", "examples/rbac_policy.csv")
+
+        // You can add custom data to a grouping policy, Casbin will ignore it. It is only meaningful to the caller.
+        // This feature can be used to store information like whether "bob" is an end user (so no subject will inherit "bob")
+        // For Casbin, it is equivalent to: e.AddGroupingPolicy("bob", "data2_admin")
+        _, _ = e.AddGroupingPolicy("bob", "data2_admin", "custom_data")
+
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "data1", "read", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "data1", "write", false)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "data2", "read", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "data2", "write", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "data1", "read", false)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "data1", "write", false)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "data2", "read", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "data2", "write", true)
+
+        // You should also take the custom data as a parameter when deleting a grouping policy.
+        // e.RemoveGroupingPolicy("bob", "data2_admin") won't work.
+        // Or you can remove it by using RemoveFilteredGroupingPolicy().
+        _, _ = e.RemoveGroupingPolicy("bob", "data2_admin", "custom_data")
+
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "data1", "read", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "data1", "write", false)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "data2", "read", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "data2", "write", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "data1", "read", false)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "data1", "write", false)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "data2", "read", false)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "data2", "write", true)
 }
 
 func TestRBACModelWithPattern(t *testing.T) {
-	e, _ := NewEnforcer("examples/rbac_with_pattern_model.conf", "examples/rbac_with_pattern_policy.csv")
-
-	// Here's a little confusing: the matching function here is not the custom function used in matcher.
-	// It is the matching function used by "g" (and "g2", "g3" if any..)
-	// You can see in policy that: "g2, /book/:id, book_group", so in "g2()" function in the matcher, instead
-	// of checking whether "/book/:id" equals the obj: "/book/1", it checks whether the pattern matches.
-	// You can see it as normal RBAC: "/book/:id" == "/book/1" becomes KeyMatch2("/book/:id", "/book/1")
-	e.AddNamedMatchingFunc("g2", "KeyMatch2", util.KeyMatch2)
-	e.AddNamedMatchingFunc("g", "KeyMatch2", util.KeyMatch2)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "any_user", "/pen3/1", "GET", true)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "/book/user/1", "/pen4/1", "GET", true)
-
-	testEnforce(t, e, "/book/user/1", "/pen4/1", "POST", true)
-
-	testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/book/1", "GET", true)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/book/2", "GET", true)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/pen/1", "GET", true)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/pen/2", "GET", false)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "/book/1", "GET", false)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "/book/2", "GET", false)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "/pen/1", "GET", true)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "/pen/2", "GET", true)
-
-	// AddMatchingFunc() is actually setting a function because only one function is allowed,
-	// so when we set "KeyMatch3", we are actually replacing "KeyMatch2" with "KeyMatch3".
-	e.AddNamedMatchingFunc("g2", "KeyMatch2", util.KeyMatch3)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/book2/1", "GET", true)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/book2/2", "GET", true)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/pen2/1", "GET", true)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/pen2/2", "GET", false)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "/book2/1", "GET", false)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "/book2/2", "GET", false)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "/pen2/1", "GET", true)
-	testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "/pen2/2", "GET", true)
+        e, _ := NewEnforcer("examples/rbac_with_pattern_model.conf", "examples/rbac_with_pattern_policy.csv")
+
+        // Here's a little confusing: the matching function here is not the custom function used in matcher.
+        // It is the matching function used by "g" (and "g2", "g3" if any..)
+        // You can see in policy that: "g2, /book/:id, book_group", so in "g2()" function in the matcher, instead
+        // of checking whether "/book/:id" equals the obj: "/book/1", it checks whether the pattern matches.
+        // You can see it as normal RBAC: "/book/:id" == "/book/1" becomes KeyMatch2("/book/:id", "/book/1")
+        e.AddNamedMatchingFunc("g2", "KeyMatch2", util.KeyMatch2)
+        e.AddNamedMatchingFunc("g", "KeyMatch2", util.KeyMatch2)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "any_user", "/pen3/1", "GET", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "/book/user/1", "/pen4/1", "GET", true)
+
+        testEnforce(t, e, "/book/user/1", "/pen4/1", "POST", true)
+
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/book/1", "GET", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/book/2", "GET", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/pen/1", "GET", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/pen/2", "GET", false)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "/book/1", "GET", false)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "/book/2", "GET", false)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "/pen/1", "GET", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "/pen/2", "GET", true)
+
+        // AddMatchingFunc() is actually setting a function because only one function is allowed,
+        // so when we set "KeyMatch3", we are actually replacing "KeyMatch2" with "KeyMatch3".
+        e.AddNamedMatchingFunc("g2", "KeyMatch2", util.KeyMatch3)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/book2/1", "GET", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/book2/2", "GET", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/pen2/1", "GET", true)
+        testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "/pen2/2", "GET", false)

+
+func TestBLPModel(t *testing.T) {
+// Check if the BLP model file exists before attempting to load
+e, err := NewEnforcer("examples/blp_model.conf", "examples/blp_policy.csv")
+if err != nil {
+This indicates the files don't exist or there's a syntax error - create basic test
+model files not initialized yet: %v", err)
+
+}
+
+// Test BLP model rules
+// Security levels: confidential < secret < top_secret
+// Alice has secret clearance, Bob has top_secret clearance
+// doc1 is confidential, doc2 is secret, doc3 is top_secret
+
+// Alice (secret) trying to read doc1 (confidential) - allowed (no read up)
+testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "doc1", "read", true)
+// Alice (secret) trying to read doc2 (secret) - allowed
+testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "doc2", "read", true)
+// Alice (secret) trying to read doc3 (top_secret) - denied (no read up)
+testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "doc3", "read", false)
+// Alice (secret) trying to write doc1 (confidential) - denied (no write down)
+testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "doc1", "write", false)
+// Alice (secret) trying to write doc2 (secret) - allowed
+testEnforce(t, e, "alice", "doc2", "write", true)
+
+// Bob (top_secret) trying to read doc1 (confidential) - allowed
+testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "doc1", "read", true)
+// Bob (top_secret) trying to read doc2 (secret) - allowed
+testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "doc2", "read", true)
+// Bob (top_secret) trying to read doc3 (top_secret) - allowed
+testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "doc3", "read", true)
+// Bob (top_secret) trying to write doc1 (confidential) - denied (no write down)
+testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "doc1", "write", false)
+// Bob (top_secret) trying to write doc2 (secret) - denied (no write down)
+testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "doc2", "write", false)
+// Bob (top_secret) trying to write doc3 (top_secret) - allowed
+testEnforce(t, e, "bob", "doc3", "write", true)
 }
